<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer12963302545995867110">Alice Bullock is a young newlywed whose husband, Charlie, has just joined the Union Army, leaving her on his Iowa farm with only his formidable mother for company. Alice writes lively letters to her sister filled with accounts of local quilting bees, the rigors of farm life, and the customs of small-town America. But no town is too small for intrigue and treachery, and whe</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12963302545995867110">Alice Bullock is a young newlywed whose husband, Charlie, has just joined the Union Army, leaving her on his Iowa farm with only his formidable mother for company. Alice writes lively letters to her sister filled with accounts of local quilting bees, the rigors of farm life, and the customs of small-town America. But no town is too small for intrigue and treachery, and when Alice finds herself accused of murder, she discovers her own hidden strengths. Rich in details of quilting, Civil War-era America, and the realities of a woman's life in the nineteenth century, <em>Alice's Tulips </em>is Sandra Dallas at her best.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12963302545995867110">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1325720671">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1325720671" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5364077-connie" class="left imgcol" title="Connie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1307502493p2/5364077.jpg" alt="Connie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1325720671?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 05, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5364077-connie" class="user" title="Connie">Connie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5364077-connie?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5364077-connie?shelf=iowa" class="actionLinkLite">iowa</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5364077-connie?shelf=war-american-civil" class="actionLinkLite">war-american-civil</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5364077-connie?shelf=summer-2015" class="actionLinkLite">summer-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1325720671">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3351719760702900892">Eighteen-year-old Alice has only been married for six months when her husband marches off to war for the Union Army. He left her on the family farm in rural Iowa with his stern mother. Alice was an immature city girl with a flirty, gregarious manner so the isolation and hard work of farm life was a big adjustment. The book is told in a series of letters to her sister, although many of them have much more dialogue than you would ever find in a normal letter. The correspondence is lively, gossipy,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3351719760702900892">Eighteen-year-old Alice has only been married for six months when her husband marches off to war for the Union Army. He left her on the family farm in rural Iowa with his stern mother. Alice was an immature city girl with a flirty, gregarious manner so the isolation and hard work of farm life was a big adjustment. The book is told in a series of letters to her sister, although many of them have much more dialogue than you would ever find in a normal letter. The correspondence is lively, gossipy, and often humorous. The letters show the lives of the women left behind as they work the farm and contribute to the war effort. As the story unfolds, Alice matures into a strong, caring young woman.<br /><br />A quilting theme runs through the book since the women would meet together to make quilts to send to the soldiers and offer emotional support to each other. A murder adds some suspense and spice since Alice is a suspect. We also learn the fates of some of the soldiers who were prisoners of war at Andersonville. The main characters worked their way into my heart so I was sorry to see the book end.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3351719760702900892">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_140485716">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/140485716" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4804005-kayla-turner" class="left imgcol" title="Kayla Turner"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1294957427p2/4804005.jpg" alt="Kayla Turner" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/140485716?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 13, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4804005-kayla-turner" class="user" title="Kayla Turner">Kayla Turner</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Nobody</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Kayla by: </span>
      My 11th grade history teacher
  </div>



    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer140485716">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15086065900157908386">This book is the most god-awful abomination on the face of the earth, next to the Twilight series. I had to read it for a history project and I was appalled. The main character Alice is a Mary-Sue. She's 100% perfect and possesses no flaws whatsoever. All the men in the town want her for themselves while her husband is at war and Alice does nothing to stop their advances. The book has no plot, even though the summary suggests otherwise. The whole "murder" theme doesn't even become apparant until</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15086065900157908386">This book is the most god-awful abomination on the face of the earth, next to the Twilight series. I had to read it for a history project and I was appalled. The main character Alice is a Mary-Sue. She's 100% perfect and possesses no flaws whatsoever. All the men in the town want her for themselves while her husband is at war and Alice does nothing to stop their advances. The book has no plot, even though the summary suggests otherwise. The whole "murder" theme doesn't even become apparant until four chapters before the book ends. Even then, nothing happens. Alice is accused of MURDER. Murder! And absolutely NOTHING happens! All her friends just quit talking to her. What a tragedy! In this era, it wouldn't have mattered if there was evidence or not. If Alice was accused, she'd be taken into custody, a trial would be held, and she'd most likely be hung. But no, Alice is perfect. Even though she clearly kills a man, she's not responsible for it. Two other women confess to clear Alice's name. It's ridiculous. <br />In addition to having no plot, there are many lewd references to sex and masturbation. Considering that the Civil War took place in the mid-Victorian era when letter-writing was an art, they did not talk about that. Ever. It just wasn't done in a society that encouraged sexual repression. My next issue with the book is the characters of Annie and Joybell. The author took the time to make them the epitome of a sterotypical southeners: uneducated, poor, and inbred. Stereotypes aren't nice Ms. Dallas.<br />Don't even bother reading this book. Seriously. Just burn it now and save yourself the trouble. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15086065900157908386">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="xhr_comment_body">

<span id="freeTextContainer4647164780906948492">Kayla I find your review interesting. Mostly for your characterization of Alice as a Mary-Sue who is 100% perfect. I find her deeply flawed, she is va</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4647164780906948492">Kayla I find your review interesting. Mostly for your characterization of Alice as a Mary-Sue who is 100% perfect. I find her deeply flawed, she is vain, flighty, and selfish. I do find, as the story progresses, that she is maturing. I have not finished the book yet, but I will say that the Victorian era played out differently in cities than in farming communities, and letters and diaries from these times reveal as much. Further, I would say that while Annie is written as both uneducated in the book sense and poor, Dallas undergirds her natural intelligence with her hard work, desire to learn, and practical knowledge which have thus far helped her to survive and helped Alice to grow in the skills she needs to survive. Where I don't necessarily disagree with you, is that this is not Dallas's strongest effort by a long shot. Just my take.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4647164780906948492">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_48534926">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/48534926" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1865671-sarah" class="left imgcol" title="Sarah"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Sarah" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/48534926?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 07, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1865671-sarah" class="user" title="Sarah">Sarah</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Sarah by: </span>
      Eunice from my knitting club
  </div>



    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer48534926">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15498795877765680855">I forgot I had this book. Now I remember why I do. I enjoy the growth and self-realization of the heroine. I like the story-telling device (her letters to her sister) and that with only a few lines we get almost a full picture of her sister's story as well. It's earthy, but I like a bit of frankness. It does remind me that for as much as we lament "society" today, I would much rather be living right when and where I am.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_792501676">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/792501676" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/12280997-carole-roman" class="left imgcol" title="Carole Roman"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442667699p2/12280997.jpg" alt="Carole Roman" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/792501676?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 17, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/12280997-carole-roman" class="user" title="Carole Roman">Carole Roman</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer792501676">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2382894651803259261">This is a great story! The character's are so real, they stay with you long after you close the book. The lost art of letter writing was how people communicated in the past. This book is a peephole into the life a young girl and we watch her grow up as war erases her youth and callowness. Realistic character, foibles and all both lovable and unforgettable. The irony in the ending is alone, worth the read. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1191693566">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1191693566" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/11869072-jeanette" class="left imgcol" title="Jeanette"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1372095557p2/11869072.jpg" alt="Jeanette" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1191693566?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 03, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/11869072-jeanette" class="user" title="Jeanette">Jeanette</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1191693566">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15059125420809334204">Civil War era novel that is comprised of letters written during the war years to the protagonist's sister, husband. It's an interesting account of having to work a farm (Iowa)without men and with a crabby mother-in-law. It certainly kept my interest and held some dicey details. But I thought that the copy in the letters was at some points not possible or highly unlikely for a woman of that period. If the author had chosen a few dramatic decisions it would have been better. She tried to do too mu</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15059125420809334204">Civil War era novel that is comprised of letters written during the war years to the protagonist's sister, husband. It's an interesting account of having to work a farm (Iowa)without men and with a crabby mother-in-law. It certainly kept my interest and held some dicey details. But I thought that the copy in the letters was at some points not possible or highly unlikely for a woman of that period. If the author had chosen a few dramatic decisions it would have been better. She tried to do too much with having nearly every scenario possible for someone close to our letter writer. It tried to do too much with the jealousy, domestic violence, drugging, cancer etc. Of course some of these would definitely have raised their nasty heads- but not all. It made our heroine so intrinsic Polyanna that I could never swallow her "eyes". Feel good historical fiction that incorporates quite a bit of revisionist insight to the main character. I like my Civil War ladies to be completely of their periods. And good sewers too. This one was half of that quantity.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_154862139">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/154862139" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3361842-keilani-ludlow" class="left imgcol" title="Keilani Ludlow"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Keilani Ludlow" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/154862139?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 16, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3361842-keilani-ludlow" class="user" title="Keilani Ludlow">Keilani Ludlow</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer154862139">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13428802145679132857">I liked Persian Pickle Club more, I liked Buster's Midnight Cafe less. I usually don't give a summary because you can read that everywhere, but I have to give a bit of one to explain what I see. The main character, Alice, is left with her cranky mother-in-law on a farm near the middle of nowhere when her husband joins up to fight for the Union. She has been married about a year and when she married him, he worked in a store. She specifically did not marry a farmer, having been raised on a farm a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13428802145679132857">I liked Persian Pickle Club more, I liked Buster's Midnight Cafe less. I usually don't give a summary because you can read that everywhere, but I have to give a bit of one to explain what I see. The main character, Alice, is left with her cranky mother-in-law on a farm near the middle of nowhere when her husband joins up to fight for the Union. She has been married about a year and when she married him, he worked in a store. She specifically did not marry a farmer, having been raised on a farm and wanting nothing to do with it. However, they end up back home helping mom-in-law with the farm and then her husband joins up. That's where the book starts. The book is written as letters to her sister. Alice starts out as a spoiled and shallow girl. She's very lightweight and not all that likable. Throughout the book, as she is forced to take on more responsibility and begins to get an idea of the plight of others, the danger her husband faces, etc. she eventually matures to a better person. Not really a much better person, but better. I enjoyed the history, the relationships she develops with others, and she is somewhat amusing so the story rolls. She's overly flirtatious which kinds of rubs me wrong. There are two instances that to me are like a sticker in your sock during a long walk. It doesn't ruin the walk, but the couple of times it pokes you make things uncomfortable and take a little something out of the story. At one point she encourages her sister to try various methods to abort her baby because she has two little ones and a third right now is just too much. Her callous and flippant disregard of the fact that she's encouraging her sister to kill her unborn baby for convenience sake really bothered me. It isn't lengthy, but it is to me, very ugly. There's also a brief reference to masturbation. Not graphic, like I said it is brief, but it also is unnecessary and vulgar to have even included. All in all it was interesting and engaging, even with the uncomfortable pokes and a main character that isn't that stellar of a person.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13428802145679132857">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1371163211">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4076592482476945033">I enjoyed this book very much. It was a quick read, as it was written in the form of letters...one sister to another. At first, I didn't like that it was only Alice writing, and never the reverse as well. However, as the book progressed, that didn't bother me anymore. It was interesting to see how Alice matured and changed over the course of the civil war and I liked how the title of the book was worked into the story. The characters of the book were interesting as well. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13841690331817791694">Alice Bullock is a young old newlywed whose husband Charlie has joined the Union Army. Alice is living with her mother-in-law on the family farm in Iowa and this book tells her story (and the story of all the characters) through letters from Alice to her sister Lizzie. Life was hard on a farm in 1862, really hard for Alice because she was not exactly the choice Mother Bullock would have made for her son, and even harder for her son as a soldier during the Civil War.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText13841690331817791694">Alice Bullock is a young old newlywed whose husband Charlie has joined the Union Army. Alice is living with her mother-in-law on the family farm in Iowa and this book tells her story (and the story of all the characters) through letters from Alice to her sister Lizzie. Life was hard on a farm in 1862, really hard for Alice because she was not exactly the choice Mother Bullock would have made for her son, and even harder for her son as a soldier during the Civil War. This book was recommended to me by one of my Goodreads friends and I was pleasantly surprised as to how much I liked it. I loved the way the story was told through the series of letters. Each letter, even the short ones, packed a wallop in it! And I learned a lot about quilts!!</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_466483074">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/466483074" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/15033381-laura" class="left imgcol" title="?Laura"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1450147821p2/15033381.jpg" alt="?Laura" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/466483074?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 08, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/15033381-laura" class="user" title="?Laura">?Laura</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/15033381-laura?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/15033381-laura?shelf=owned-books" class="actionLinkLite">owned-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/15033381-laura?shelf=on-kindle" class="actionLinkLite">on-kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer466483074">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11944241870318682162">I really liked this book. It's a nice, quiet little read with likable characters for whom you hope against hope things will turn out well. I liked that it was composed entirely of letters written from Alice to her sister. Alice's voice was enjoyable and she interjected subtle humor into much of her writing. She reminded me somewhat of Scarlet O'Hara in the way that she matured over the course of the book. Having read <a title="The Diary of Mattie Spenser by Sandra Dallas" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/360992.The_Diary_of_Mattie_Spenser">The Diary of Mattie Spenser</a>, I appreciated the references to characters from th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11944241870318682162">I really liked this book. It's a nice, quiet little read with likable characters for whom you hope against hope things will turn out well. I liked that it was composed entirely of letters written from Alice to her sister. Alice's voice was enjoyable and she interjected subtle humor into much of her writing. She reminded me somewhat of Scarlet O'Hara in the way that she matured over the course of the book. Having read <a title="The Diary of Mattie Spenser by Sandra Dallas" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/360992.The_Diary_of_Mattie_Spenser">The Diary of Mattie Spenser</a>, I appreciated the references to characters from that story and look forward to reading more from Sandra Dallas, as I suspect some references were to characters from other of her books. The information on quilting at the start of each chapter was a nice little bonus to this book and helped to provide context. I definitely recommend this book.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11944241870318682162">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18177992493821318768"><br />Alice's Tulips is another fine Sandra Dallas book. The plot is simplistic: women on their own, trying to farm and survive during the war between the states. Both there is nothing simplistic about the hardships that Alice and her mother-in-law faced.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText18177992493821318768"><br />Alice's Tulips is another fine Sandra Dallas book. The plot is simplistic: women on their own, trying to farm and survive during the war between the states. Both there is nothing simplistic about the hardships that Alice and her mother-in-law faced. The two plucky women made their way and found room for others. Yet again, Sandra Dallas has intertwined information and a love of quilting as an integral part of the story. I was again struck by the honest, open view Sandra gives of small town life, with all its prejudices with people from away and the changing factions within a town when gossip is one of the prime commodities. I suspect the universality of small town life will be recognized by many.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1499739550">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1499739550" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/13507335-chloe-c" class="left imgcol" title="Chloe C"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Chloe C" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1499739550?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 07, 2016</a>

      <a href="/user/show/13507335-chloe-c" class="user" title="Chloe C">Chloe C</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1499739550">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17878756058345475216">“Alice’s Tulips” by Sandra Dallas is the story of a young girl named Alice Bullock. Her husband has just been sent off to war, and now Alice lives on a farm with her stern mother-in-law. The story is told through letters from Alice to her sister Lizzie, and for the most part I enjoyed this format. It was fun and full of gossip which I enjoyed reading. It made the historical fiction a little easier to bear. However, the book took a while to pick up. It wasn’t until the end of the novel that Alice</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17878756058345475216">“Alice’s Tulips” by Sandra Dallas is the story of a young girl named Alice Bullock. Her husband has just been sent off to war, and now Alice lives on a farm with her stern mother-in-law. The story is told through letters from Alice to her sister Lizzie, and for the most part I enjoyed this format. It was fun and full of gossip which I enjoyed reading. It made the historical fiction a little easier to bear. However, the book took a while to pick up. It wasn’t until the end of the novel that Alice is accused of murder, and the drama really picked up. Before that point, the story consisted of the gossip of a typical woman during the civil-war era. Therefore the book really had no plot, but that all changed when Alice was accused of murder. Though it was a turn for the worst in the book, considering most of it was innocent fun up until then, the murder trial really brought out the true colors of all the characters. For example, Mother Bullock vouched for her daughter-in-law after all the time of bickering and not getting along and Alice’s true friends, Nealie and Annie, stick up for her as well. Overall, I didn’t mind reading this book, as it was fun to watch the characters and relationships grow. That is why I am rating this book a 4. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17878756058345475216">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a href="/review/show/1247838008?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 06, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/39013290-kylee-peterson" class="user" title="Kylee Peterson">Kylee Peterson</a>

          added it




        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/39013290-kylee-peterson?shelf=ya-13-25" class="actionLinkLite">ya-13-25</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1247838008">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12457243243455338087">Alice is a mere 18 years old when she marries Charlie, who soon leaves to fight in for the Union in the Civil War. Immature and stubborn Alice is left to live with her brand new mother in law, Mother Bullock, where they must learn to work together and Alice must learn to grow up. In a series of letters to her sister Lizzie, the details of Alice’s new life are disclosed: her hardships, flirtations, quilting, and relationship with Charlie’s mother are all analyzed as they evolve through the space</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12457243243455338087">Alice is a mere 18 years old when she marries Charlie, who soon leaves to fight in for the Union in the Civil War. Immature and stubborn Alice is left to live with her brand new mother in law, Mother Bullock, where they must learn to work together and Alice must learn to grow up. In a series of letters to her sister Lizzie, the details of Alice’s new life are disclosed: her hardships, flirtations, quilting, and relationship with Charlie’s mother are all analyzed as they evolve through the space of the war. It also explores the hardships of the Civil War through the eyes of her beloved Charlie in his occasional correspondence. As hardships ensue, Alice finds herself in the midst of a murder mystery and must defend herself and learn to grow through her trials. <br />I loved the letter format of this novel, the way it allowed me to see through Alice’s eyes and get to know her character so intimately made her transformation throughout the book all the more dramatic. I also thought the way that Sandra Dallas wove actual quilting patterns and techniques into the story added an element of uniqueness and made the novel seem even more realistic. The contrast between life at war and life at home was fascinating as well, although I may be biased towards this book because I am a bit of a Civil War buff. I didn’t love some of the vulgarity of the novel, but aside from that I really did enjoy the dynamic characters and Alice’s passionately personal story. Content to be wary of includes sexuality and vulgar language. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12457243243455338087">...more</a>

  <a href="/user/show/9919989-olivermagnus" class="left imgcol" title=" Olivermagnus  "><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1406988553p2/9919989.jpg" alt=" Olivermagnus  " /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a href="/review/show/1014152769?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 02, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/9919989-olivermagnus" class="user" title=" Olivermagnus  "> Olivermagnus  </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/9919989-olivermagnus?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1014152769">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16602328340481238260">When her husband enlists as a Union soldier, teenage newlywed Alice Bullock must live on his family's Bramble Farm on the outskirts of Slatyfork, Iowa, with only her stern mother-in-law for company. The story is told through Alice’s letters to her sister over two and a half years, and are filled with accounts of quilting bees, the hardness of farm life, and small town customs. In her long, gossipy letters to Lizzie we experience Alice's life on the run-down farm. As the story unfolds, secrets an</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16602328340481238260">When her husband enlists as a Union soldier, teenage newlywed Alice Bullock must live on his family's Bramble Farm on the outskirts of Slatyfork, Iowa, with only her stern mother-in-law for company. The story is told through Alice’s letters to her sister over two and a half years, and are filled with accounts of quilting bees, the hardness of farm life, and small town customs. In her long, gossipy letters to Lizzie we experience Alice's life on the run-down farm. As the story unfolds, secrets and mysteries flourish, and Alice shares every joy and sorrow with her sister by letter. The farm is falling apart, there is little food to eat, squatters are living on her property, her horse is dying and she is constantly being scolded. She misses her husband desperately and fears he may never return from the war. <br /><br />The letters portray a growing up period for Alice as she changes from a young bride to a woman who has responsibility over the lives of others. Alice likes to have a good time, and admits to be very vain about her sewing and quilting skills. Her only happiness is when she takes up her needle to sew and quilt. This pastime is one of her remedies for those lonely nighttime hours stuck inside the small house. As Alice faces life’s challenges and becomes the main suspect in a local murder she re-examines her relationship with Mother Bullock. Their growing mutual respect forms the core of a novel about the realities of a woman’s life in Civil War era America. The last third of the novel is a subtle balance between sentiment and tragedy and I couldn't put it down.<br /><br />This was my first Sandra Dallas novel and I enjoyed it so much. If you have an interest in both historical fiction and quilting you will get even more enjoyment from this book. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16602328340481238260">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer48272978">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13751576913110924860">This is one of my favourite books. Set during the American civil war, it's about the relationship between a young war bride and her mother-in-law, and a coming of age story. Told through letters sent to her sister, mother, and new husband, we see the evolution of a young girl into a young woman. It is wonderfully sculpted and beautifully told, with a very distinct voice. I loved this book, and often buy it to give to girlfriends for birthdays or other occasions. </span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16630015222964094022">Fun read. Set during the Civil War and written as a series of letters to protagonists sister. Has a bit of suspense to make it fun. <span id="freeTextContainer1232934417194556358">The history told in this book about the Civil War era was fascintating.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText13892522245797288465">A very slow beginning and middle. I enjoy the format of letter writing but it's been mostly the story of a self-centered teenager (married woman of the 1800s) who has to move to her husband's farm while he is off serving in the Civil War. She grows up quite a bit in the two years he is gone which has been interesting enough to keep me going but it has been slow going. A third of the book left and something is finally happening. Because of my growing interest at this point I'm not sure if it's worth 3 stars or the 2 I would have previously given.<br /><br />Update: I enjoyed the end of this book. I wish the first 2-quarters had been a more interesting read but I was satisfied with the outcome.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer203099603">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11803905889869987974">I would say maybe even 3.5 stars. I have liked other books by Sandra Dallas better than this one--although I couldn't put it down. I think it's because I like Dallas' other books so much that I was hopeful that it would get better--and it did. As in the Persian Pickle Club, there are many quilting references. Even for a non-quilter--I really liked that. <br /><br />The book is written in first person by Alice, and it is all written in the style of letters to her sister. I really enjoy that style of writing.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11803905889869987974">I would say maybe even 3.5 stars. I have liked other books by Sandra Dallas better than this one--although I couldn't put it down. I think it's because I like Dallas' other books so much that I was hopeful that it would get better--and it did. As in the Persian Pickle Club, there are many quilting references. Even for a non-quilter--I really liked that. <br /><br />The book is written in first person by Alice, and it is all written in the style of letters to her sister. I really enjoy that style of writing. I did not like a lot of the main characters at all at the beginning. I disliked Alice the most. She was uppity, selfish, and liked to flirt with other gentlemen while her husband was away serving in the Union army. I also did not like the occasional lewd comments regarding marital relations that Alice wrote about. But I hoped that this book would follow Alice's "maturing" and it did. Alice ended up being more selfless and caring. <br /><br />Not a bad book, but not my favorite either. But it didn't deter me from reading more of Sandra Dallas. On to another book today from her. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11803905889869987974">...more</a>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer222038508">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2442629718671544953">Story of the young wife of a civil war soldier that is written in the form of letters to her sister. I really liked it at first (thus 2 stars rather than 1). I loved the language and the naivety of the heroine as she has to get along with her mother-in-law and the townspeople after husband leaves to fight.<br /><br />But the voice of the story changed as it progressed. It became more mundane and the heroine's behavior became annoying. Then towards the end there is a plot event that changes the story entirel</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2442629718671544953">Story of the young wife of a civil war soldier that is written in the form of letters to her sister. I really liked it at first (thus 2 stars rather than 1). I loved the language and the naivety of the heroine as she has to get along with her mother-in-law and the townspeople after husband leaves to fight.<br /><br />But the voice of the story changed as it progressed. It became more mundane and the heroine's behavior became annoying. Then towards the end there is a plot event that changes the story entirely. It was foreshadowed and handled well, but for some reason it completely destroyed my interest. I didn't want the story to go that direction (it's so hard to talk about this without giving away any spoilers) and that it did so ruined the book for me. I put it down (weeks ago), intending to go back and finish it, but I have no desire to do so. Which is weird. I'm not sure I've ever made it so far into a book (3/4 point) and just not cared about the ending.<br /><br />Either way, there are better books out there.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_606470760">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/606470760" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7976144-kim-overstreet" class="left imgcol" title="Kim Overstreet"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1410564729p2/7976144.jpg" alt="Kim Overstreet" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/606470760?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 03, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7976144-kim-overstreet" class="user" title="Kim Overstreet">Kim Overstreet</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer606470760">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16102516722464741839">I have read almost all of Sandra Dallas' novels and often find myself reaching for one on a rainy day or when I am sick and want something easy to read, cozy, and riveting all at the same time. Alice's Tulips, a novel told through a series of letters, is the story of Alice, a young bride left on a farm with her stern mother-in-law when her husband joins the Union Army during the Civil War. Alice is spunky, funny, and quite likable. Through her letters, Dallas captures many of the hardships women</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16102516722464741839">I have read almost all of Sandra Dallas' novels and often find myself reaching for one on a rainy day or when I am sick and want something easy to read, cozy, and riveting all at the same time. Alice's Tulips, a novel told through a series of letters, is the story of Alice, a young bride left on a farm with her stern mother-in-law when her husband joins the Union Army during the Civil War. Alice is spunky, funny, and quite likable. Through her letters, Dallas captures many of the hardships women faced in the era. Each chapter began with a brief quilting blurb, which tied in with the letters that followed. I am not a quilter, but enjoyed reading the historical tidbits. For the most part, the letters work well as a storytelling device, though some passages don't come across as entirely authentic - for example, when Alice describes her appearance to her sister or recounts an entire conversation verbatim, though as a reader I was glad for the information! I expected a murder mystery from the book's description. There is a murder, but it plays a lesser role in the story than Alice's growth as a woman. I will enthusiastically recommend Alice's Tulips and all of Sandra Dallas' work to quilters and fans of female-centered historical fiction such as that written by Jennifer Chiaverini and Tracy Chevalier. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16102516722464741839">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12139143758754579305">This book is about a newlywed named Alice, she lives with her husband's mother on Bramble Farm during the Civil war era. During the story she is accused of murder and is shunned from society in the town of Slatyfork. The entire book is letters to her sister.<br />When I first read what this book was about I thought this might be good. I thought there would be more action with the murder but I was wrong. I even tried to like Alice but that was nearly impossible. She was a terrible person. She told her</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12139143758754579305">This book is about a newlywed named Alice, she lives with her husband's mother on Bramble Farm during the Civil war era. During the story she is accused of murder and is shunned from society in the town of Slatyfork. The entire book is letters to her sister.<br />When I first read what this book was about I thought this might be good. I thought there would be more action with the murder but I was wrong. I even tried to like Alice but that was nearly impossible. She was a terrible person. She told her husband that he should only come back if he can still dance, who says that to a person when they are going to fight in a war! She also is obsessed with being better than Jeannie Kate. She would constantly remind everyone that her quilting was superior to Jeannie Kate's. She held a grudge against Jeannie Kate even after she <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[died <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but she took her child anyway. The only reason Alice didn't like Jeannie Kate was because she liked Alice's husband, Charlie. Well Alice, I don't understand why other people can't like Charlie. I understand he is your husband but well since Charlie choose you over Jeannie Kate you have nothing to worry about!<br />Then other part that bothered me was that she didn't kill anyone until more than halfway through the book! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ Then at the end it turned out that she didn't even kill the guy! Annie did and that Mother Bullock died lying for Alice.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />The only character I actually liked was Mother Bullock. I don't know how she could stand living with Alice. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[I can't believe she lied for her on her deathbed and it turned out that she had been lying for the wrong person! I nearly cried when Mother Bullock died and if I didn't have to finish this book I would have stopped right there.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />I would not recommend this book to anyone unless they <em>really</em> like history books.<!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>

          <a href="/book/show/1293638.Alice_s_Tulips" title="Hardcover 9780312203597" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer152601386">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2732340998854732158">I feel like I should give this book a higher rating to spite the people who gave it low ratings because they're convinced that no one spoke or, thought of, or even had sex before the 1960s. And the people who think that saying a girl's skirt was pushed up and her legs spread constitutes a "horrifically graphic rape scene." Please, Jack Weyland writes more graphically than that.<br /><br />But frankly speaking, the book is just bland. Descriptions of the serial rapist's actions and the justice delivered to h</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2732340998854732158">I feel like I should give this book a higher rating to spite the people who gave it low ratings because they're convinced that no one spoke or, thought of, or even had sex before the 1960s. And the people who think that saying a girl's skirt was pushed up and her legs spread constitutes a "horrifically graphic rape scene." Please, Jack Weyland writes more graphically than that.<br /><br />But frankly speaking, the book is just bland. Descriptions of the serial rapist's actions and the justice delivered to him are done quite in keeping with the time period and as tastefully as possible considering the subject matter. And the idea that a seventeen-year-old newlywed would not be interested in and enjoy sex is ludicrous. Of course she's going to confide in her sister, and the roundabout way she does is exactly what one would expect. Of course . . . everything about this book is pretty much exactly what one would expect, from the first sentence to the last. Hence, the blandness.<br /><br />The quilting trivia was really interesting though. Worth a read just for that. If you're into that sort of historical trivia, anyway.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer50516612">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6143203582216276626">This is a wonderful story written in the form of letters sent from Alice to her sister. The book takes place during the civil war and starts with a newly wed Alice saying good-bye to her husband Charley as he heads to war, fighting on the side of the North.<br /><br />She is left at home on the small family farm, with just her and her mother-in-law.<br /><br />Through her letters to her sister we see how Alice grows and changes from an immature, vain little flirt, to a stronger and wiser young woman.<br /><br />There is more viole</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6143203582216276626">This is a wonderful story written in the form of letters sent from Alice to her sister. The book takes place during the civil war and starts with a newly wed Alice saying good-bye to her husband Charley as he heads to war, fighting on the side of the North.<br /><br />She is left at home on the small family farm, with just her and her mother-in-law.<br /><br />Through her letters to her sister we see how Alice grows and changes from an immature, vain little flirt, to a stronger and wiser young woman.<br /><br />There is more violence in this book that the others I have read by Sandra Dallas and I was a little surprised by the discussion of sex and very intimate details of her sex life she shared with her sister in her letters, especially considering that this book takes place during the end of the Victorian era.<br /><br />But, all in all I enjoyed this book and was very moved and touched by the story and the characters.<br /><br />As always I just have to say, Sandra Dallas is a wonderful story teller!</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }
  }

Turner continues Sarah\'s extraordinary story as she struggles to make a home in the Arizona Territory.It is winter 1906, and nearing bankruptcy after surviving drought, storms, and the rustling of her cattle, Sarah remains a stalwart pillar to her extended family. Then a stagecoach accident puts in her path three strangers who will change her life.In sickness and in health, neighbor Udell Hanna remains a trusted friend, pressing for Sarah to marry. When he reveals a plan to grant Sarah her dearest wish, she is overwhelmed with passion and excitement. She soon discovers, however, that there is more to a formal education than she bargained for.Behind the scenes, Sarah\'s old friend Maldonado has struck a deal with the very men who will become linchpins of the Mexican Revolution. Maldonado plots to coerce Sarah into partnership, but when she refuses, he devises a murderous plan to gain her land for building a railroad straight to Mexico. When Sarah\'s son Charlie unexpectedly returns from town with a new bride, the plot turns into an all-out range war between the two families.Finally putting an end to Udell\'s constant kindnesses, Sarah describes herself as &amp;quot;an iron-boned woman.&amp;quot; She wants more than to be merely a comfortable fill-in for his dead wife. Strong-willed Southern belle Mary Bullitt abandons her life of luxury in Louisville, Kentucky, when she marries General Henry Atkinson and accompanies him to his outpost on the Mississippi. Nothing has prepared her for marriage to this attractive older man -- or for the realities of frontier living. Conditions are primitive, Mary knows virtually nothing about her husband, and the threat of attack from Indians is constant. A rough and resourceful general, Henry is engaged in a long and historic clash with a great Native American leader, and his deeply conflicted feelings about Indians mirror those he and his wife have for each other.  In the tradition of Willa Cather and Edna Ferber, Micaela Gilchrist has crafted an exciting novel that is at once a love story and an action-packed depiction of the struggle for the     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/74078.Sandra_Dallas">About Sandra Dallas</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/74078.Sandra_Dallas"><img alt="74078" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1276294358p2/74078.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer8197725895192627736">Award-winning author SANDRA DALLAS was dubbed “a quintessential American voice” by Jane Smiley, in Vogue Magazine. Sandra’s novels with their themes of loyalty, friendship, and human dignity have been translated into a dozen foreign languages and have been optioned for films.<br /><br />A journalism graduate of the University of Denver, Sandra began her writing career as a reporter with Business Week. A staff</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8197725895192627736">Award-winning author SANDRA DALLAS was dubbed “a quintessential American voice” by Jane Smiley, in Vogue Magazine. Sandra’s novels with their themes of loyalty, friendship, and human dignity have been translated into a dozen foreign languages and have been optioned for films.<br /><br />A journalism graduate of the University of Denver, Sandra began her writing career as a reporter with Business Week. A staff member for twenty-five years (and the magazine’s first female bureau chief,) she covered the Rocky Mountain region, writing about everything from penny-stock scandals to hard-rock mining, western energy development to contemporary polygamy. Many of her experiences have been incorporated into her novels. <br /><br />While a reporter, she began writing the first of ten nonfiction books. They include Sacred Paint, which won the National Cowboy Hall of Fame Western Heritage Wrangler Award, and The Quilt That Walked to Golden, recipient of the Independent Publishers Assn. Benjamin Franklin Award.<br /><br />Turning to fiction in 1990, Sandra has published eight novels, including Prayers For Sale. Sandra is the recipient of the Women Writing the West Willa Award for New Mercies, and two-time winner of the Western Writers of America Spur Award, for The Chili Queen and Tallgrass. In addition, she was a finalist for the Colorado Book Award, the Mountain and Plains Booksellers Assn. Award, and a four-time finalist for the Women Writing the West Willa Award.<br /><br />The mother of two daughters—Dana is an attorney in New Orleans and Povy is a photographer in Golden, Colorado—Sandra lives in Denver with her husband, Bob.<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/sandradallas" target="_blank">http://us.macmillan.com/author/sandra...</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8197725895192627736">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/74078.Sandra_Dallas" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Sandra Dallas...</a>
